<content>The Rik Khan or Khan Ming ceremony is one of the most important national ceremonies of the Ahom people. This event is organized to empower one or more individuals or a country or nation. The Tai Ahom believe that many &amp;#39;khans&amp;#39; are associated with a person, which keeps him healthy and full of vitality. When a person falls into water or suffers from a serious illness, panics or suffers from depression or fear of severe force, or suddenly becomes restless and tired, that person loses some &amp;#39;khun&amp;#39; There are many descriptions of &amp;#39;rik-khan&amp;#39; or life-giving ceremonies in Ahom history. According to folk belief, the &amp;#39;khans&amp;#39; released from the body and mind of a person in such states go to rivers, seas, forests, mountains, tall trees, fruit trees like oranges, etc., and take refuge in the sky. The Ahom celebrate the &amp;#39;Khun&amp;#39; Ming&amp;#39; or &amp;#39;Rik Khan&amp;#39; ceremony with the aim of bringing back these abandoned &amp;#39;Khuns&amp;#39; During the reign of the Ahom kings, the &amp;#39;Rikkhan,&amp;#39; or &amp;#39;Khanming&amp;#39; ceremony was celebrated with royal pomp before the army left for battle, after its return from battle and during the coronation of the prince. The royal priests also performed this ceremony to gather the people to fight against the enemy and to strengthen the king before his coronation</content>

</page>

<page>
<page_no> 328  </page_no>
<content>328 Visvan or Khun Ming (lifting of life) was celebrated. This program attempts to bring back the &amp;#39;Khans who have left their body and mind and taken refuge in the splendor of nature. Lost &amp;#39;khans&amp;#39; are called &amp;#39;khantuks&amp;#39; (in humans). In the case of individuals, the ceremony celebrated to save the blood is called &amp;#39;Ao Rin Ming&amp;#39; or &amp;#39;Khunming&amp;#39; or &amp;#39;Rik Khun&amp;#39; In the case of the country or nation, this revival ceremony is called &amp;#39;Rik-khun Myung&amp;#39; The &amp;#39;Rik Khan&amp;#39; or &amp;#39;Khun Ming&amp;#39; ceremony is an essential part of the Ahom wedding ceremony &amp;#39;Chaklang&amp;#39; The &amp;#39;Khun Ming&amp;#39; ceremony is held two days before the wedding to wish the bride and groom good health. Rik literally means &amp;#39;call or invoke&amp;#39; and &amp;#39;khun&amp;#39; means &amp;#39;longevity or revival&amp;#39;.” The ritual performed for the welfare of the people of the state was called “Bishan Myungkhunban”. The ritual is usually not held after Kali Puja, ie during the dry season, as there is a shortage of water for this ritual The Ahom history records that the Ahom princes celebrated the &amp;#39;Rikshan&amp;#39; ceremony during the coronation of new kings, military victories or possible danger When King Landon sent his grandsons Khun Lung and Khun Lai to rule the earth, he said, &amp;#39;There are different communities in the earth</content>

<page_no> 344  </page_no>
<content>Chapter Fifteen The Story of the Buddhist Jataka in the Tai-Ahom Language The Buddhist Jataka is found in the form of sealed books among the Tai-Ahom scriptures. These books record the story of the Buddha&amp;#39;s previous birth. These rebirth stories are in the Ahom language and many people try to say that the Ahom were Buddhists. Since the Tai language books of Jataka stories are not kept or read as religious scriptures in any puja, we think that these Jataka stories were brought by the newly arrived Tai Khans after the arrival of Chu-ka-pha with their daughters married by the Ahom kings. These Jataka stories show the belief in reincarnation. However, the Ahom did not believe in reincarnation in the beginning. Therefore, these scriptures are written in the Ahom-Tai language but are outside the Ahom thought. To show what is written in these charts, the Assamese translations of the two charts, Nemi Mang Phura and Urak Fla Kla, are given below. In the past, when the Lord rested in a kingdom called Mithila, Clare preached his religion among the people of Mithila.</content>

</page>

The Ahom people were influenced by Hindu priests and other influential circles who gained royal favor and imposed restrictions on marriage, eating and drinking. As a result of this conversion to Hinduism or Aryanism, the royally favored priesthood identified the Tai Ahom deity Fa-nuru Landon with Indra, Jachingpha as Saraswati, Lankuri as Shiva and invented a new interpretation of the origin of the Swargadevas. However, some have become Buddhists and have participated in the worship of the gods and goddesses of the original religion. There is no place for sacrifice in Furalung Puja. Therefore, some Ahoms are trying to call it Buddhism. However, people are slowly becoming attracted to the old Ahom religion Banfi Furalung Therefore, a revival took place and the Ahom worshiped Khaokham and Landon.
